# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive `answer.json` file with all the findings related to the Kubernetes CronJob API migration from v1beta1 to batch/v1.

## Summary of Findings

The file contains:

**16 files** including:
- API type definitions (v1, v1beta1, internal batch types)
- Conversion functions (auto-generated for both v1 and v1beta1)
- Defaulting logic (with differences in pointer allocation approach)
- Validation code (including the new TimeZone field validation)
- Registry and storage implementations

**30+ symbols** documenting:
- `Convert_v1_CronJob_To_batch_CronJob` and reverse conversions for both v1 and v1beta1
- `SetDefaults_CronJob` functions showing differences between versions
- `ValidateCronJobCreate`, `ValidateCronJobUpdate`, and `validateTimeZone` validation functions
- Type definitions for CronJob and CronJobSpec

**Key findings**:
1. **TimeZone field**: Defined in both v1 and v1beta1 at protobuf bytes 8, allowing optional timezone specification for cron schedules
2. **Validation changes**: The `validateTimeZone()` function validates timezone names against IANA database standards and rejects deprecated TZ/CRON_TZ environment variables in schedules
3. **Defaulting differences**: v1 uses modern `ptr.To()` utilities while v1beta1 uses manual pointer allocation, though both set identical defaults
4. **Conversion**: Auto-generated conversion functions handle bidirectional conversion between external API versions (v1, v1beta1) and internal batch representation
5. **Deprecation**: v1beta1 is marked as deprecated (1.21) with removal planned for 1.25

The answer.json file is ready at `/workspace/answer.json`.

Generated defaults are in `zz_generated.defaults.go` files for both versions, with `SetObjectDefaults_CronJob` also calling `SetDefaults_PodSpec` on the job template.\\n\\n### Validation\\n\\n`pkg/apis/batch/validation/validation.go` implements critical validation logic:\\n\\n**ValidateCronJobCreate** (line 715): Validates CronJob on creation, checking metadata and calling `validateCronJobSpec`.\\n\\n**ValidateCronJobUpdate** (line 730): Validates CronJob updates, comparing old and new specs and calling `validateCronJobSpec`.\\n\\n**validateCronJobSpec** (line 740): Core validation that checks the spec, including schedule validation and TimeZone handling.\\n\\n**validateTimeZone** (line 816): Validates the TimeZone field by:\\n1.
